        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96040723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9700935039747991956">I loved this book from the start. The writing style is right up my alley, appropriately descriptive without being excessive, with lots of dialogue. This was my first novel from the Egyptian culture and the days of the great rulers. I wondered what I would think of such a storyline. I found I loved it!<br/><br/>This is the story of Princess Nefertari, most of the storyline taking place before she became queen. The author took a lot of liberties with the storyline, since there are so many gaps in Egyptian h</span>
  <span id="freeText9700935039747991956" style="display:none">I loved this book from the start. The writing style is right up my alley, appropriately descriptive without being excessive, with lots of dialogue. This was my first novel from the Egyptian culture and the days of the great rulers. I wondered what I would think of such a storyline. I found I loved it!<br /><br />This is the story of Princess Nefertari, most of the storyline taking place before she became queen. The author took a lot of liberties with the storyline, since there are so many gaps in Egyptian history. In this story, Nefertari is the niece of the deceased Queen Nefertiti, who was viewed, along with her husband, the Egyptian Pharaoh Akhenaten, as a heretic for turning against the Egyptian gods and worshiping only the sun god Aten.<br /><br />So when Princess Nefertari becomes the wife of Pharaoh Ramesses II, the people and court are not happy with a relative of Nefertiti on the throne, as Nefertari is cursed to carry her family's reputation as a "heretic". However with the support of Ramesses' aunt Woserit, a high priestess, and driven by a fiery and determined nature that takes her into battle with her husband, Nefertari goes on to become the queen of Egypt, and known by the people as the Warrior Queen instead of the Heretic Queen.<br /><br />This was a very enjoyable read, full of adventure and excitement and intrigue. I would highly recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9700935039747991956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16355543210646074099">Very disappointing. One of the things I enjoy most about reading historical fiction is being immersed in worlds of the past. Moran fails completely at this, she was never able to bring Ancient Egypt alive.<br/><br/>After thinking on this for a little bit, I think was really bothered me was the theme of the book - you are never good enough for the man you love, you have to change into something you aren't. The main character starts out beautiful, smart, speaks 6 or 7 languages, and is best friends with the</span>
  <span id="freeText16355543210646074099" style="display:none">Very disappointing. One of the things I enjoy most about reading historical fiction is being immersed in worlds of the past. Moran fails completely at this, she was never able to bring Ancient Egypt alive.<br /><br />After thinking on this for a little bit, I think was really bothered me was the theme of the book - you are never good enough for the man you love, you have to change into something you aren't. The main character starts out beautiful, smart, speaks 6 or 7 languages, and is best friends with the future pharaoh of Egypt. But that isn't good enough to snare this good friend as a husband - she must completely remake herself into something even more beautiful and perfect. She must never complain to him, she must always be polite and gracious, she must always dress to the nines. Only by becoming something completely different can she find true love.<br /><br />And this wonderful story line is set against a blah, cookie-cutter background.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16355543210646074099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780307381767" href="/book/show/6416651-the-heretic-queen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149112326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11290787471904398648">A vast improvement over the author's earlier Egyptian historical fiction novel, <i>Nefertiti</i>. I admit that I had low expectations for this going in, but the plot, the character's struggles (especially Nefertari's for identity and recognition, as opposed to her "aunt"'s for just power/a man) were handled much more maturely and wholly.<br/><br/><i>This</i> foray into the fascinating world of Egypt's past has a lot more to recommend it than <i>Nefertiti</i>. The characters are more accessible and rounded; the similarities (b</span>
  <span id="freeText11290787471904398648" style="display:none">A vast improvement over the author's earlier Egyptian historical fiction novel, <i>Nefertiti</i>. I admit that I had low expectations for this going in, but the plot, the character's struggles (especially Nefertari's for identity and recognition, as opposed to her "aunt"'s for just power/a man) were handled much more maturely and wholly.<br /><br /><i>This</i> foray into the fascinating world of Egypt's past has a lot more to recommend it than <i>Nefertiti</i>. The characters are more accessible and rounded; the similarities (both real and imagined by the author) between Nefertari and Nefertiti's lives are alluded to with subtlety, not obvious and overdone as I feared. I am pleasantly surprised and may even read the author's third Egyptian historical fiction, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6340471.Cleopatra_s_Daughter" title="Cleopatra's Daughter by Michelle Moran" rel="nofollow noopener">Cleopatra's Daughter</a>
</i>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11206915753193044778">The HERETIC QUEEN at its heart is a love story told from the view point of Nefertari. It is also a tale about two queens vying of the heart of Pharaoh Ramesses and who will be his ruling queen.<br/><br/>Michelle Moran does a wonderful job of transporting the reader to the intricacies of ancient Egypt, with its court politics, palaces, and the way royalty lived. I did find it slow in the beginning but it still held my interest enough to keep reading on. Nefertari is a sympathetic character who was smart, d</span>
  <span id="freeText11206915753193044778" style="display:none">The HERETIC QUEEN at its heart is a love story told from the view point of Nefertari. It is also a tale about two queens vying of the heart of Pharaoh Ramesses and who will be his ruling queen.<br /><br />Michelle Moran does a wonderful job of transporting the reader to the intricacies of ancient Egypt, with its court politics, palaces, and the way royalty lived. I did find it slow in the beginning but it still held my interest enough to keep reading on. Nefertari is a sympathetic character who was smart, determined, honest, yet naive at times and passionate about what she wanted, I couldn't help but root for her and hope she was successful.<br /><br />The HERETIC QUEEN is an interesting story of a princess’ rise to power and coming of age story. If you enjoy ancient Egyptian history, especially one that deals with strong women, then I think you will enjoy this book. <br /><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69112466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15219783720540515571">90210 goes to Egypt!! That about sums it up. I found this novel to be juvenile. The entire novel is a cat fight between Nefertari (the daughter of Mutny, Nefertiti's sister) and a harem girl named Iset. Both Nefertari and Iset become wives of Ramses II and they are constantly fighting to be Chief Wife. While Ramses jumps bed to bed impregnating one or the other, the women resort to poision, lies, and use all their charms to lure the pharoah. There is some war thrown in here and there for good me</span>
  <span id="freeText15219783720540515571" style="display:none">90210 goes to Egypt!! That about sums it up. I found this novel to be juvenile. The entire novel is a cat fight between Nefertari (the daughter of Mutny, Nefertiti's sister) and a harem girl named Iset. Both Nefertari and Iset become wives of Ramses II and they are constantly fighting to be Chief Wife. While Ramses jumps bed to bed impregnating one or the other, the women resort to poision, lies, and use all their charms to lure the pharoah. There is some war thrown in here and there for good measure and even a chapter of pirates but the constant "love' drama had me picturing Tori and Tiffani with hennaed breasts fighting over Brian Austin Green wearing a golden pectorial. Michelle has a good writing style, but I enjoyed her "Nefertiti" more and the Mutny character from it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15219783720540515571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2x1wXxV6NxcTjOL9jP6DJ94yxtArQLLYP34mKTMIBwRfxm3pI+3w74lTDpRKI0h3VPsr6gc5asqhLD0e6wOg2Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xxLUi9bj/1XFwuDQ1A3kTWcZ2vX720qRd/4G5GR0KEBDyck94HQ4rV8dDLkS0C8d7dA3z9eikoPprB3TvH+PnQ==')})
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_18667964'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18667964-daughter-of-the-gods?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Daughter of the Gods: A Novel of Ancient Egypt<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/6526628.Stephanie_Thornton?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Stephanie  Thornton<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.12 avg rating &mdash; 1,347 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2014\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer9286507020928037096\">Egypt, 1400s BC. The pharaoh’s pampered second daughter, lively, intelligent Hatshepsut, delights in racing her chariot through the marketplace and testing her archery skills in the Nile’s marshlands. But the death of her elder sister, Neferubity, in<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9286507020928037096\" style=\"display:none\">Egypt, 1400s BC. The pharaoh’s pampered second daughter, lively, intelligent Hatshepsut, delights in racing her chariot through the marketplace and testing her archery skills in the Nile’s marshlands. But the death of her elder sister, Neferubity, in a gruesome accident arising from Hatshepsut’s games forces her to confront her guilt...and sets her on a profoundly changed course. Hatshepsut enters a loveless marriage with her half brother, Thut, to secure his claim to the Horus Throne and produce a male heir. But it is another of Thut’s wives, the commoner Aset, who bears him a son, while Hatshepsut develops a searing attraction for his brilliant adviser Senenmut. And when Thut suddenly dies, Hatshepsut becomes de facto ruler, as regent to her two-year-old nephew. Once, Hatshepsut anticipated being free to live and love as she chose. Now she must put Egypt first. Ever daring, she will lead a vast army and build great temples, but always she will be torn between the demands of leadership and the desires of her heart. And even as she makes her boldest move of all, her enemies will plot her downfall....Once again, Stephanie Thornton brings to life a remarkable woman from the distant past whose willingness to defy       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/269069.Michelle_Moran">About Michelle Moran</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/269069.Michelle_Moran"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1370383933p3/269069.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/269069.Michelle_Moran">Michelle Moran

<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11352939540544558163"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a></i> <br/><br/>Michelle Moran is the international bestselling author of six historical novels, including Madame Tussaud, which was optioned for a mini-series in 2011. Her books have been translated into more than twenty languages.<br/><br/>A native of southern California, Michelle attended Pomona </span>
  <span id="freeText11352939540544558163" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a></i> <br /><br />Michelle Moran is the international bestselling author of six historical novels, including Madame Tussaud, which was optioned for a mini-series in 2011. Her books have been translated into more than twenty languages.<br /><br />A native of southern California, Michelle attended Pomona College, then earned a Masters Degree from the Claremont Graduate University. During her six years as a public high school teacher, she used her summers to travel around the world, and it was her experiences as a volunteer on archaeological digs that inspired her to write historical fiction. <br /><br />In 2012 Michelle was married in India, inspiring her seventh book, Rebel Queen, which is set in the East. Her hobbies include hiking, traveling, and archaeology. She is also fascinated by archaeogenetics, particularly since her children's heritages are so mixed. But above all these things, Michelle is passionate about reading, and can often be found with her nose in a good book. A frequent traveler, she currently resides with her husband, son, and daughter in the US.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11352939540544558163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
